README.md:Faster inference using GPU/CUDA is also supported. Compile from source with `cmake -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release  -DENABLE_CUDA=1 -DCUDAToolkit_ROOT=Path-To-Cuda-Toolkit` and call with `createdb/easy-search --prostt5-model weights --gpu 1`.
CMakeLists.txt:set(ENABLE_CUDA 0 CACHE BOOL "Enable CUDA")
CMakeLists.txt:if(ENABLE_CUDA)
CMakeLists.txt:    if(NOT DEFINED CUDAToolkit_ROOT)
CMakeLists.txt:        message(FATAL_ERROR "please set -DCUDAToolkit_ROOT=path-to-cuda")
CMakeLists.txt:    set(CANDLE_FEATURE cuda)
CMakeLists.txt:    if(ENABLE_CUDA)
CMakeLists.txt:        corrosion_set_env_vars(cprostt5 CUDA_ROOT=${CUDAToolkit_ROOT})

lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs://! Exposes [CudaTypeName] which maps between rust type names
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs://! and the corresponding cuda kernel type names.
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs://! For example, `f32` in rust corresponds to `float` in a cuda
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:/// Maps a rust type to it's corresponding [CudaTypeName::NAME] in cuda c++ land.
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:pub trait CudaTypeName {
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:macro_rules! cuda_type {
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:    ($RustTy:ty, $CudaTy:expr) => {
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:        impl CudaTypeName for $RustTy {
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:            const NAME: &'static str = $CudaTy;
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(bool, "bool");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(i8, "char");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(i16, "short");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(i32, "int");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(i64, "long");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(isize, "intptr_t");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(u8, "unsigned char");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(u16, "unsigned short");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(u32, "unsigned int");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(u64, "unsigned long");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(usize, "size_t");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(f32, "float");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/types.rs:cuda_type!(f64, "double");

lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! 1. [CUDA driver API](https://docs.nvidia.com/cuda/cuda-driver-api/index.html)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! 2. [NVRTC API](https://docs.nvidia.com/cuda/nvrtc/index.html)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! 3. [cuRAND API](https://docs.nvidia.com/cuda/curand/index.html)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! 4. [cuBLAS API](https://docs.nvidia.com/cuda/cublas/index.html)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! 1. [`driver::CudaDevice`] is a handle to a specific device ordinal (e.g. 0, 1, 2, ...)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! 2. [`driver::CudaSlice<T>`], which represents a [`Vec<T>`] on the device, can be allocated
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://!    using the aforementioned CudaDevice.
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! Here is a table of similar concepts between CPU and Cuda:
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! | Concept | CPU | Cuda |
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! | Memory allocator | [`std::alloc::GlobalAlloc`] | [`driver::CudaDevice`] |
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! | List of values on heap | [`Vec<T>`] | [`driver::CudaSlice<T>`] |
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! | Slice | `&[T]` | [`driver::CudaView<T>`] |
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! | Mutable Slice  | `&mut [T]` | [`driver::CudaViewMut<T>`] |
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! | Function | [`Fn`] | [`driver::CudaFunction`] |
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! | Thread | [`std::thread::Thread`] | [`driver::CudaStream`] |
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! be loaded into a device with [`driver::CudaDevice::load_ptx()`].
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! [cublas::CudaBlas] can perform gemm operations using [`cublas::Gemm<T>`],
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! allocated by the driver in the form of: [`driver::CudaSlice<T>`],
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! [`driver::CudaView<T>`], and [`driver::CudaViewMut<T>`].
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/lib.rs://! [curand::CudaRng] can fill a [`driver::CudaSlice<T>`] with random data, based on

lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! For some operations, it is necessary to only operate on a small part of a single [CudaSlice].
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! Use [CudaSlice::try_slice()] and [CudaSlice::try_slice_mut()] for this. The returned
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! views ([CudaView] and [CudaViewMut] hold references to the owning [CudaSlice],
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! These view structs can be used with [CudaFunction].
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! # use cudarc::{driver::*, nvrtc::*};
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! # let device = CudaDevice::new(0).unwrap();
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! let mut a: CudaSlice<f32> = device.alloc_zeros::<f32>(3 * 10).unwrap();
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://!     let mut a_sub_view: CudaViewMut<f32> = a.try_slice_mut(i_batch * 10..).unwrap();
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://!     let f: CudaFunction = device.get_func("module_name", "my_function").unwrap();
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! It would be possible to re-use [CudaSlice] itself for sub-slices, however that would involve adding
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! In order to use a [CudaDevice] on multiple threads, you must call [CudaDevice::bind_to_thread] on
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! control when [CudaDevice] can be dropped.
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! This is accomplished by putting all of them inside one struct, the [CudaDevice]. There are other ways,
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! Additionally, [CudaDevice] implements [Drop] as releasing all the data from the device in
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! The next part of safety is ensuring that [CudaSlice] do not outlive
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! the [CudaDevice]. For usability, each [CudaSlice] owns an `Arc<CudaDevice>`
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/cudarc/src/driver/mod.rs://! Multi stream is supported via [CudaStream], however it automatically

lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:# Bindgen Cuda
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:[![Latest version](https://img.shields.io/crates/v/bindgen_cuda.svg)](https://crates.io/crates/bindgen_cuda)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:[![Documentation](https://docs.rs/bindgen_cuda/badge.svg)](https://docs.rs/bindgen_cuda)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:![License](https://img.shields.io/crates/l/bindgen_cuda.svg)
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:It will help create automatic bindgen to cuda kernels source files and make them easier to use
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:`src/cuda.cu`
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:```cuda
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:__global__ void cuda_hello(){
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:    printf("Hello World from GPU!\n");
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:You can add `bindgen_cuda` as a build dependency:
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:cargo add --build bindgen_cuda
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:    let builder = bindgen_cuda::Builder::default();
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:pub const CUDA: &str = include_str!(concat!(env!("OUT_DIR"), "/cuda.ptx"));
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:You can then use the PTX directly in your rust code with a library like [cudarc](https://github.com/coreylowman/cudarc/).
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:## Raw cuda calls
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:Alternatively you can build a static library that you can link against in build.rs in order to call cuda directly with the c code.
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/bindgen_cuda/README.md:`src/cuda.cu`

lib/prostt5/c/vendor/safetensors/README.md:- Zero-copy: No format is really zero-copy in ML, it needs to go from disk to RAM/GPU RAM (that takes time). On CPU, if the file is already in cache, then it can
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/safetensors/README.md:truly be zero-copy, whereas on GPU there is not such disk cache, so a copy is always required
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/safetensors/README.md:GPU loading times are as fast or faster than PyTorch equivalent.
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/safetensors/README.md:Loading first on CPU with memmapping with torch, and then moving all tensors to GPU seems
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/safetensors/README.md:- Lazy loading: in distributed (multi-node or multi-gpu) settings, it's nice to be able to
lib/prostt5/c/vendor/safetensors/README.md:to load the model on 8 GPUs from 10mn with regular PyTorch weights down to 45s.
